1:4:91:45:36:81:377:444:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:Gustavo Berganti ̃nos and Juan Vidal-Puga

2:9:268:0:33:113:481:645:21:g_d0_f6:21:g_d0_f6:One-way and two-way cost allocation in hub
2:10:310:33:0:223:370:612:21:g_d0_f6:21:g_d0_f6:network problems
2:11:326:0:48:370:377:620:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:∗
2:12:327:48:30:177:416:572:14:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f9:G. Berganti ̃nos†1and J. Vidal-Puga‡1
2:13:364:30:29:123:470:542:10:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f8:1Departamento de Estat ́ıstica e Investigaci ́on Operativa,
2:14:423:29:43:210:384:513:14:g_d0_f8:14:g_d0_f8:Universidade de Vigo, Spain
2:15:450:43:61:242:352:470:14:g_d0_f8:14:g_d0_f8:November 2, 2016
2:16:466:61:25:273:321:409:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:Abstract
2:17:474:25:17:148:462:384:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:We study hub problems where a set of nodes send and receive data
2:18:538:17:18:132:462:367:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:from each other. In order to reduce costs, the nodes use a network with
2:19:609:18:17:132:462:349:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:a given set of hubs.  We address the cost sharing aspect by assuming
2:20:677:17:18:132:462:332:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:that nodes are only interested in either sending or receiving data, but
2:21:748:18:18:132:462:314:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:not both (one-way flow) or that nodes are interested in both sending
2:22:816:18:17:132:462:296:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:and receiving data (two-way flow).  In both cases, we study the non-
2:23:884:17:18:132:462:279:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:emptiness of the core and the Shapley value of the corresponding cost
2:24:953:18:17:132:160:261:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:game.
2:25:958:17:18:148:447:244:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f9:Keywords:hub network, cost allocation, core, Shapley value.
2:26:1017:18:19:116:491:226:7:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f9:∗This work is partially supported by research grants ECO2014-52616-R from the Span-
2:27:1100:19:16:102:491:207:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:ish Ministerio de Econom ́ıa y Competitividad, GRC 2015/014 from Xunta de Galicia, and
2:28:1186:16:9:102:370:191:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:19320/PI/14 from Fundaci ́on S ́eneca de la Regi ́on de Murcia.
2:29:1249:9:13:116:237:182:7:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f9:†E-mail:  gbergant@uvigo.es
2:30:1276:13:0:116:241:169:7:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f9:‡E-mail:  vidalpuga@uvigo.es
3:31:1305:0:31:102:238:701:17:g_d0_f12:17:g_d0_f12:1    Introduction
3:32:1322:31:19:102:491:670:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Hub networks play a fundamental role in modeling telecommunication, trans-
3:33:1396:19:19:102:491:651:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:portation, and parcel delivery systems.  Assume that there are users located
3:34:1472:19:18:102:491:632:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:at different geographical nodes who need to send a certain flow of data or
3:35:1546:18:19:102:491:614:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:goods to each other through costly connections.  A planner needs to locate
3:36:1620:19:19:102:491:595:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:an optimal number of hub facilities at some nodes so that each other node is
3:37:1696:19:19:102:491:576:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:connected to exactly one hub and all the hubs are connected to one another
3:38:1770:19:18:102:491:557:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:at  a  reduced  cost  (due  to  economies  of  scale).   Hence,  the  optimal  flow  of
3:39:1857:18:19:102:491:539:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:data/goods between any pair of origin-destination nodes has a length of at
3:40:1931:19:19:102:491:520:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:most four:  It must go from the point of origin to its assigned hub (when the
3:41:2008:19:19:102:491:501:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:origin is not itself a hub), then to the hub assigned to the destination (if it is
3:42:2090:19:19:102:491:482:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:a different node) and finally to the destination (again, if it is not itself a hub).
3:43:2174:19:18:102:491:463:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:This topology is applied to Internet connections (Bailey, 1997), telecommu-
3:44:2249:18:19:102:491:445:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:nications between local networks (Greenfield, 2000), satellite communication
3:45:2325:19:19:102:491:426:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:(Helme  and  Magnanti,  1989),  airline  networks  (Bryan  and  O’Kelly,  1999;
3:46:2404:19:19:102:403:407:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Yang, 2009), and small package delivery (Sim et al., 2009).
3:47:2463:19:18:120:491:388:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Several classes of hub problems have been studied.  We mention some of
3:48:2533:18:19:102:491:370:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:them.  Aykin (1994) considers that hubs have limited capacities and direct
3:49:2607:19:19:102:491:351:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:connections between nohubs are allowed.  Ernst and Krishnamoorthy (1999)
3:50:2679:19:19:102:491:332:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:consider the case where there are capacity restrictions but they apply only
3:51:2754:19:19:102:491:313:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:to the traffic arriving at hubs from nohubs.  Sasaki and Fukushima (2003)
3:52:2827:19:18:102:491:294:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:consider  the  case  where  there  are  capacity  constraints  on  hubs  and  arcs.
3:53:2910:18:19:102:491:276:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Labb ́e et al. (2005) consider the case where each hub has a limited capacity
3:54:2987:19:19:102:491:257:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:as regard the traffic that passes through it.  The main issue addressed in these
3:55:3067:19:19:102:491:238:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:papers  is  the  study  of  algorithms  for  computing  optimal  ways  of  sending
3:56:3149:19:18:102:491:219:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:goods  between  the  nodes  in  such  a  way  that  the  total  cost  is  minimized.
3:57:3233:18:19:102:491:201:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Of course the location of the hubs plays a relevant role in the minimization
3:58:3309:19:19:102:491:182:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:problem.  See Alumur and Kara (2008) and Farahani et al. (2013) for surveys
3:59:3384:19:19:102:192:163:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:on this literature.
3:60:3403:19:19:120:491:144:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Another interesting question is how to divide the cost of sending the good
3:61:3477:19:0:102:491:125:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:from one node to another.  This question has been successfully addressed in
4:62:3553:0:19:102:491:701:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:several kinds of problem.  We mention some of them:  Guardiola et al. (2009)
4:63:3629:19:19:102:491:682:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:study  production-inventory  problems  where  players  share  production  pro-
4:64:3707:19:19:102:491:663:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:cesses  and  warehouse  facilities,  Berganti ̃nos  and  Kar  (2010),  Bogomolnaia
4:65:3789:19:18:102:491:644:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:and Moulin (2010), Dutta and Mishra (2012) and Trudeau (2012, 2014) con-
4:66:3861:18:19:102:491:626:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:sider the cost of connecting agents to a source, Moulin (2014) consider users
4:67:3938:19:19:102:491:607:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:that need to connect a pair of target nodes in a network, and Alcalde-Unzu
4:68:4012:19:19:102:491:588:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:et al. (2015) consider the cost of cleaning a river.  However, few papers have
4:69:4090:19:19:102:491:569:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:studied  this  issue  in  hub  problems.   We  mention  three:  in  all  of  them  the
4:70:4176:19:18:102:491:550:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:first step is to consider a class of hub problems,  the next is to associate a
4:71:4254:18:19:102:491:532:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:cooperative  game  with  each  problem  in  the  class,  and  the  last  is  to  study
4:72:4340:19:19:102:491:513:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:the core of such problems.  If the core is non empty, an allocation in the core
4:73:4419:19:19:102:470:494:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:could be considered as a nice way of sharing the cost among the agents.
4:74:4490:19:18:120:491:475:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Skorin-Kapov  (1998)  studiesp-hub  allocation  problems,  wherephubs
4:75:4559:18:19:102:491:457:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:must be optimally allocated.  Several cooperative games are considered de-
4:76:4633:19:19:102:491:438:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:pending on who the agents are (nodes or pairs of nodes) and what coalitions
4:77:4708:19:19:102:491:419:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:can do (whether they must use the optimal network for the whole problem
4:78:4779:19:19:102:491:400:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:or can construct the optimal network of the reduced problem induced by the
4:79:4853:19:18:102:491:381:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:coalition).  The core of such games is studied.  Some games have an empty
4:80:4926:18:19:102:481:363:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:core but others do not.  Finally, the nucleolus of such games is considered.
4:81:5002:19:19:120:491:344:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Skorin-Kapov  (2001)  studies  hub-like  networks,  which  involves  ap-hub
4:82:5077:19:19:102:491:325:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:median problem where direct connection between nodes is possible.  More-
4:83:5149:19:19:102:491:306:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:over, there are savings when the traffic is high.  He defines several associated
4:84:5229:19:18:102:491:287:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:cooperative games where the set of agents are the links.  He shows that some
4:85:5305:18:19:102:491:269:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:of them can have an empty core, in other cases the core is a singleton, and
4:86:5380:19:19:102:275:250:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:in other cases it has many points.
4:87:5414:19:19:120:491:231:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Matsubayashi et al. (2005) consider the case where the number of hubs
4:88:5483:19:18:102:491:212:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:to  be  located  is  arbitrary;  there  is  a  cost  of  opening  a  hub  and  there  is  a
4:89:5574:18:19:102:491:194:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:congestion cost associated with nodes (the greater the flow through a node,
4:90:5649:19:19:102:491:175:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:the greater its cost).  They also define an associated cooperative game and
4:91:5724:19:19:102:491:156:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:study its core.  In the cooperative game the players are the nodes and the
4:92:5798:19:0:102:491:137:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:characteristic function is defined assuming that each coalition cooperatively
5:93:5876:0:19:102:491:701:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:constructs a network to minimize the total cost associated with hubs in the
5:94:5951:19:19:102:491:682:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:coalition and communications initiated also by nodes in the coalition.  More-
5:95:6028:19:19:102:491:663:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:over, each coalition simply assumes that the rest of the nodes do not establish
5:96:6107:19:18:102:491:644:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:any hub nodes and the coalition can determine the routing of all the traffic
5:97:6183:18:19:102:491:626:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:generated by the other nodes.  Given this, they prove that the core could be
5:98:6259:19:19:102:491:607:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:empty, but they find a sufficient condition for the non-emptiness of the core
5:99:6336:19:19:102:407:588:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:and propose an allocation in the core when it is non-empty.
5:100:6395:19:19:120:491:569:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Our also focuses on the cost sharing issue.  We consider two cases.  In the
5:101:6470:19:18:102:491:550:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:first case (called one-way flow) we assume, as in Skorin-Kapov (1998, 2001)
5:102:6545:18:19:102:491:532:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:and  Matsubayashi  et  al.  (2005),  that  nodes  are  only  interested  in  sending
5:103:6629:19:19:102:491:513:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:flow.   In  the  second  case  (called  two-way  flow)  we  assume  that  agents  are
5:104:6714:19:19:102:491:494:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:interested  in  both  sending  and  receiving  flow.   Internet  connections  are  a
5:105:6798:19:18:102:348:475:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:good example of situations covered by this case.
5:106:6846:18:19:120:491:457:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We  study  the  existence  of  core  allocations  and,  unlike  Skorin-Kapov
5:107:6922:19:19:102:491:438:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:(1998,  2001)  and  Matsubayashi  et  al.  (2005),  we  also  present  and  charac-
5:108:7005:19:19:102:491:419:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:terize two rules that belong to the core and also satisfy other nice properties.
5:109:7085:19:19:120:491:400:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We now summarize our results for one-way flow.  We consider two cooper-
5:110:7156:19:18:102:491:381:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:ative games associated with each hub problem and related to those presented
5:111:7231:18:19:102:491:363:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:by Skorin-Kapov (1998).  In the first game we assume that nodes can only use
5:112:7307:19:19:102:491:344:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:the optimal network for the whole problem.  In the second game we consider
5:113:7381:19:19:102:491:325:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:that nodes can construct their own optimal networks.  In both games, when
5:114:7454:19:19:102:491:306:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:we compute the cost of a coalition we consider only the flow sent by nodes
5:115:7528:19:18:102:183:287:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:in the coalition.
5:116:7545:18:19:120:491:269:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We study the cores of both games.  The core of the first game has many
5:117:7615:19:19:102:491:250:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:points.  In any allocation in the core each node pays the cost of sending its
5:118:7692:19:19:102:491:231:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:flow and the cost of any hub is divided in any way among the nodes that use
5:119:7767:19:18:102:491:212:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:such hub.  The core of the second game could be empty.  In particular, we
5:120:7840:18:19:102:491:194:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:prove that the Shapley value corresponds to the allocation where each node
5:121:7914:19:19:102:491:175:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:pays the cost of sending its flow and the cost of any hub is divided equally
5:122:7990:19:19:102:491:156:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:among the nodes that use it.  Thus, the Shapley value belongs to the core.
5:123:8064:19:0:102:491:137:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We also provide two axiomatic characterizations of it.  The first one uses core
6:124:8144:0:19:102:491:701:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:selection (the allocation must be in the core) and equal treatment on hubs
6:125:8218:19:19:102:491:682:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:(if the cost of a hub increases then any pair of agents such that either both
6:126:8295:19:19:102:491:663:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:need the hub or neither needs the hub are affected in the same way).  The
6:127:8368:19:18:102:491:644:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:second  characterization  uses  positivity  (no  node  can  obtain  profits),  equal
6:128:8452:18:19:102:491:626:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:treatment on hubs, independence of irrelevant hubs (nodes are not affected
6:129:8526:19:19:102:491:607:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:by a change in the cost of hubs that they do not need), and independence of
6:130:8601:19:19:102:491:588:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:irrelevant flows (if the flow between two nodes increases, other agents should
6:131:8679:19:19:102:186:569:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:not be affected).
6:132:8696:19:18:120:491:550:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We now summarize our results for the two-way flow.  The study is similar
6:133:8768:18:19:102:491:532:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:to the one-way flow.  We associate two games.  The first game is concave and
6:134:8844:19:19:102:491:513:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:hence its core is non empty.  It consists of the convex hull of the vector of
6:135:8921:19:19:102:453:494:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:marginal contributions.  The second game could have an empty core.
6:136:8987:19:18:120:491:475:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We study the Shapley value of the first game.  Since the game is concave
6:137:9059:18:19:102:491:457:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:it belongs to the core.  We prove that the Shapley value corresponds to the
6:138:9134:19:19:102:491:438:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:allocation where the cost of sending flow between any pair of nodes is divided
6:139:9212:19:19:102:491:419:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:equally between the two nodes.  Moreover,  the cost of each hub is divided
6:140:9286:19:19:102:491:400:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:equally between the nodes that need the hub to send or receive their flows.
6:141:9361:19:18:102:491:381:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Finally, we provide two axiomatic characterizations.  The first one uses core
6:142:9438:18:19:102:491:363:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:selection, equal treatment on hubs, and equal treatment on flows (if there is a
6:143:9517:19:19:102:491:344:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:flow between a pair of nodes and it increases then both nodes must be affected
6:144:9595:19:19:102:491:325:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:in the same way).  The second characterization uses positivity, independence
6:145:9671:19:19:102:491:306:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:of irrelevant hubs, independence of irrelevant flows, equal treatment on hubs,
6:146:9749:19:18:102:255:287:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:and equal treatment on flows.
6:147:9778:18:19:120:491:269:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:The paper is organized as follows.  Section 2 presents the model.  Section 3
6:148:9854:19:19:102:491:250:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:studies the one-way flow case, where the nodes are only interested in sending
6:149:9931:19:19:102:491:231:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:or  receiving  flow,  but  not  both.   Section  4  studies  the  two-way  flow  case,
6:150:10017:19:0:102:441:212:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:where the nodes are interested in both sending and receiving flow.
7:151:10084:0:31:102:222:701:17:g_d0_f12:17:g_d0_f12:2    The model
7:152:10098:31:19:102:491:670:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:We consider situations where a group of agents, located at different points,
7:153:10174:19:19:102:491:651:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:want to send and receive some specific good, which is sent through a costly
7:154:10249:19:18:102:491:632:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:network.  Besides, we could locate some hubs in the agent’s points.  All hub
7:155:10325:18:19:102:491:614:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:agents are connected among them but each non-hub agent is connected to
7:156:10395:19:19:102:393:595:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:only a hub agent.  We now introduce the model formally.
7:157:10450:19:19:120:418:576:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:N={1,...,n}is a finite set of nodes (also called agents).
7:158:10507:19:18:120:491:557:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:C= (cij)i,j∈Nis a cost matrix.  For eachi,j∈N, cijis the cost of sending
7:159:10579:18:19:102:491:539:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:a unit of flow from nodeito nodej.  We assumecii= 0,cij=cji≥0 and
7:160:10644:19:19:102:264:520:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:cik≤cij+cjkfor alli,j,k∈N.
7:161:10670:19:19:120:491:501:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:F= (fij)i,j∈Nis the flow matrix.  For eachi,j∈N,fijrepresents the
7:162:10735:19:19:102:491:482:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:amount of flow from nodeito nodej.  We assumefij≥0 andfii= 0 for
7:163:10799:19:18:102:491:463:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:alli,j∈N.   Notice  that  we  do  not  assumefij=fji,i.e.the  flow  is  not
7:164:10874:18:19:102:217:445:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:necessarily symmetric.
7:165:10896:19:19:120:491:426:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:d=  (di)i∈Nindicates  the  cost  of  maintaining  or  constructing  a  hub  at
7:166:10974:19:19:102:324:407:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:each node.  We assumedi≥0 for alli∈N.
7:167:11011:19:18:120:491:388:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:α∈[0,1] is the discounting factor of the cost when flow goes between a
7:168:11081:18:19:102:491:370:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:pair of hubs.  Namely, ifiandjare both hubs, then the cost of sending a
7:169:11152:19:19:102:342:351:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:unit of flow fromitojisαcij(instead ofcij)1.
7:170:11196:19:19:120:491:332:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:The first issue is to locate an optimal number of hubs, selected from the set
7:171:11273:19:19:102:491:313:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:of nodes.  Besides, each non-hub is linked to exactly one hub and all the hubs
7:172:11351:19:18:102:491:294:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:are connected to each other.  The triangular inequationcik≤cij+cjkassures
7:173:11424:18:19:102:491:276:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:that the optimal path origin-destination uses at most two hubs.  When there
7:174:11499:19:19:102:491:257:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:is a hub in nodei∈N, we say with some abuse of notation that nodeiis a
7:175:11569:19:19:102:355:238:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:hub.  Otherwise, we say that nodeiis a non-hub.
7:176:11616:19:18:120:491:219:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:Ahub  networkonNis  determined  by  a  nonempty  setH⊆Nand  a
7:177:11677:18:19:102:490:201:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:functionh:N\H−→Hsuch thath(i) is the hub linked to non-hubi.  Let
7:178:11742:19:19:102:490:182:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f8:Hbe the set of all hub networks onN.  For notational convenience, we write
7:179:11816:19:19:102:491:163:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:h(i) =iwheni∈H, so thathis a function fromNontoH.  Besides, we
7:180:11878:19:19:116:491:144:7:g_d0_f18:10:g_d0_f9:1A generalization would be to assume that these costs are given by another cost matrix
7:181:11964:19:0:102:126:125:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f9:Ch=

7:186:11983:0:0:201:404:129:7:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f9:hij≤cijfor alli,j∈N.  In our case,Ch=αC.

10:301:14939:46:31:102:245:584:17:g_d0_f12:17:g_d0_f12:3    One-way flow
10:302:14956:31:19:102:491:553:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:In this section,  we assume that agents are interested only in the flow that

24:1533:32371:19:19:102:491:241:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:receiving and sending data.  Again, we assume that communication is carried
24:1534:32446:19:19:102:491:222:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:over a (maybe optimal) hub network.  We first associate to each hub network
24:1535:32521:19:18:102:491:203:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:problem a cooperative game.  Later on we study the core and the Shapley
24:1536:32592:18:19:102:132:185:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:value.
24:1537:32598:19:19:120:491:166:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:For each hub network problemPwe associate the cost gamectfhwhere
24:1538:32662:19:19:102:491:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:for eachS⊆N,ctfh(S) is the cost of sending and receiving the flow of all
24:1539:32734:19:0:102:491:128:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:agents  inSto  and  from  all  agents  throughh.   The  cost  gamectfhmodels
25:1540:32812:0:19:102:491:701:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:situations  where  an  (optimal)  hub  networkh(with  associated  set  of  hubs
25:1541:32891:19:19:102:491:682:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f8:H) has already been constructed.  Thus,dcould be considered as a vector of
25:1542:32965:19:19:102:491:663:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:maintenance costs.  Agents in each coalition are interested in the hubs they
25:1543:33041:19:18:102:491:644:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:need  for  sending  or  receiving  their  flow.   Notice  that  we  are  applying  the
25:1544:33127:18:19:102:491:626:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:same ideas than in the one-way flow.  We now define this cost game formally.
25:1545:33203:19:19:120:491:607:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:For eachS⊆N, letHtfS⊆Hdenote the set of hubs needed for sending
